{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01NHocTykN1S1LxEsKqmxLCy","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: # gRPCurl\\n2: [![Build Status](https://circleci.com/gh/fullstorydev/grpcurl/tree/master.svg?style=svg)](https://circleci.com/gh/fullstorydev/grpcurl/tree/master)\\n3: [![Go Report Card](https://goreportcard.com/badge/github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl)](https://goreportcard.com/report/github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl)\\n4: \\n5: `grpcurl` is a command-line tool that lets you interact with gRPC servers. It's\\n6: basically `curl` for gRPC servers.\\n7: \\n8: The main purpose for this tool is to invoke RPC methods on a gRPC server from the\\n9: command-line. gRPC servers use a binary encoding on the wire\\n10: ([protocol buffers](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/), or \\\"protobufs\\\"\\n11: for short). So they are basically impossible to interact with using regular `curl`\\n12: (and older versions of `curl` that do not support HTTP/2 are of course non-starters).\\n13: This program accepts messages using JSON encoding, which is much more friendly for both\\n14: humans and scripts.\\n15: \\n16: With this tool you can also browse the schema for gRPC services, either by querying\\n17: a server that supports [server reflection](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/master/src/proto/grpc/reflection/v1alpha/reflection.proto),\\n18: by reading proto source files, or by loading in compiled \\\"protoset\\\" files (files that contain\\n19: encoded file [descriptor protos](https://github.com/google/protobuf/blob/master/src/google/protobuf/descriptor.proto)).\\n20: In fact, the way the tool transforms JSON request data into a binary encoded protobuf\\n21: is using that very same schema. So, if the server you interact with does not support\\n22: reflection, you will either need the proto source files that define the service or need\\n23: protoset files that `grpcurl` can use.\\n24: \\n25: This repo also provides a library package, `github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl`, that has\\n26: functions for simplifying the construction of other command-line tools that dynamically\\n27: invoke gRPC endpoints. This code is a great example of how to use the various packages of\\n28: the [protoreflect](https://godoc.org/github.com/jhump/protoreflect) library, and shows\\n29: off what they can do.\\n30: \\n31: See also the [`grpcurl` talk at GopherCon 2018](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dDr-8kbMnaw).\\n32: \\n33: ## Features\\n34: `grpcurl` supports all kinds of RPC methods, including streaming methods. You can even\\n35: operate bi-directional streaming methods interactively by running `grpcurl` from an\\n36: interactive terminal and using stdin as the request body!\\n37: \\n38: `grpcurl` supports both secure/TLS servers _and_ plain-text servers (i.e. no TLS) and has\\n39: numerous options for TLS configuration. It also supports mutual TLS, where the client is\\n40: required to present a client certificate.\\n41: \\n42: As mentioned above, `grpcurl` works seamlessly if the server supports the reflection\\n43: service. If not, you can supply the `.proto` source files or you can supply protoset\\n44: files (containing compiled descriptors, produced by `protoc`) to `grpcurl`.\\n45: \\n46: ## Installation\\n47: \\n48: ### Binaries\\n49: \\n50: Download the binary from the [releases](https://github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl/releases) page.\\n51: \\n52: ### Homebrew (macOS)\\n53: \\n54: On macOS, `grpcurl` is available via Homebrew:\\n55: ```shell\\n56: brew install grpcurl\\n57: ```\\n58: \\n59: ### Docker\\n60: \\n61: For platforms that support Docker, you can download an image that lets you run `grpcurl`:\\n62: ```shell\\n63: # Download image\\n64: docker pull fullstorydev/grpcurl:latest\\n65: # Run the tool\\n66: docker run fullstorydev/grpcurl api.grpc.me:443 list\\n67: ```\\n68: Note that there are some pitfalls when using docker:\\n69: - If you need to interact with a server listening on the host's loopback network, you must specify the host as `host.docker.internal` instead of `localhost` (for Mac or Windows) _OR_ have the container use the host network with `-network=\\\"host\\\"` (Linux only).\\n70: - If you need to provide proto source files or descriptor sets, you must mount the folder containing the files as a volume (`-v $(pwd):/protos`) and adjust the import paths to container paths accordingly.\\n71: - If you want to provide the request message via stdin, using the `-d @` option, you need to use the `-i` flag on the docker command.\\n72: \\n73: ### Other Packages\\n74: \\n75: There are numerous other ways to install `grpcurl`, thanks to support from third parties that\\n76: have created recipes/packages for it. These include other ways to install `grpcurl` on a variety\\n77: of environments, including Windows and myriad Linux distributions.\\n78: \\n79: You can see more details and the full list of other packages for `grpcurl` at _repology.org_:\\n80: https://repology.org/project/grpcurl/information\\n81: \\n82: ### From Source\\n83: If you already have the [Go SDK](https://golang.org/doc/install) installed, you can use the `go`\\n84: tool to install `grpcurl`:\\n85: ```shell\\n86: go install github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl/cmd/grpcurl@latest\\n87: ```\\n88: \\n89: This installs the command into the `bin` sub-folder of wherever your `$GOPATH`\\n90: environment variable points. (If you have no `GOPATH` environment variable set,\\n91: the default install location is `$HOME/go/bin`). If this directory is already in\\n92: your `$PATH`, then you should be good to go.\\n93: \\n94: If you have already pulled down this repo to a location that is not in your\\n95: `$GOPATH` and want to build from the sources, you can `cd` into the repo and then\\n96: run `make install`.\\n97: \\n98: If you encounter compile errors and are using a version of the Go SDK older than 1.13,\\n99: you could have out-dated versions of `grpcurl`'s dependencies. You can update the\\n100: dependencies by running `make updatedeps`. Or, if you are using Go 1.11 or 1.12, you\\n101: can add `GO111MODULE=on` as a prefix to the commands above, which will also build using\\n102: the right versions of dependencies (vs. whatever you may already have in your `GOPATH`).\\n103: \\n104: ## Usage\\n105: The usage doc for the tool explains the numerous options:\\n106: ```shell\\n107: grpcurl -help\\n108: ```\\n109: \\n110: In the sections below, you will find numerous examples demonstrating how to use\\n111: `grpcurl`.\\n112: \\n113: ### Invoking RPCs\\n114: Invoking an RPC on a trusted server (e.g. TLS without self-signed key or custom CA)\\n115: that requires no client certs and supports server reflection is the simplest thing to\\n116: do with `grpcurl`. This minimal invocation sends an empty request body:\\n117: ```shell\\n118: grpcurl grpc.server.com:443 my.custom.server.Service/Method\\n119: \\n120: # no TLS\\n121: grpcurl -plaintext grpc.server.com:80 my.custom.server.Service/Method\\n122: ```\\n123: \\n124: To send a non-empty request, use the `-d` argument. Note that all arguments must come\\n125: *before* the server address and method name:\\n126: ```shell\\n127: grpcurl -d '{\\\"id\\\": 1234, \\\"tags\\\": [\\\"foo\\\",\\\"bar\\\"]}' \\\\\\n128:     grpc.server.com:443 my.custom.server.Service/Method\\n129: ```\\n130: \\n131: As can be seen in the example, the supplied body must be in JSON format. The body will\\n132: be parsed and then transmitted to the server in the protobuf binary format.\\n133: \\n134: If you want to include `grpcurl` in a command pipeline, such as when using `jq` to\\n135: create a request body, you can use `-d @`, which tells `grpcurl` to read the actual\\n136: request body from stdin:\\n137: ```shell\\n138: grpcurl -d @ grpc.server.com:443 my.custom.server.Service/Method <<EOM\\n139: {\\n140:   \\\"id\\\": 1234,\\n141:   \\\"tags\\\": [\\n142:     \\\"foor\\\",\\n143:     \\\"bar\\\"\\n144:   ]\\n145: }\\n146: EOM\\n147: ```\\n148: \\n149: ### Listing Services\\n150: To list all services exposed by a server, use the \\\"list\\\" verb. When using `.proto` source\\n151: or protoset files instead of server reflection, this lists all services defined in the\\n152: source or protoset files.\\n153: ```shell\\n154: # Server supports reflection\\n155: grpcurl localhost:8787 list\\n156: \\n157: # Using compiled protoset files\\n158: grpcurl -protoset my-protos.bin list\\n159: \\n160: # Using proto sources\\n161: grpcurl -import-path ../protos -proto my-stuff.proto list\\n162: ```\\n163: \\n164: The \\\"list\\\" verb also lets you see all methods in a particular service:\\n165: ```shell\\n166: grpcurl localhost:8787 list my.custom.server.Service\\n167: ```\\n168: \\n169: ### Describing Elements\\n170: The \\\"describe\\\" verb will print the type of any symbol that the server knows about\\n171: or that is found in a given protoset file. It also prints a description of that\\n172: symbol, in the form of snippets of proto source. It won't necessarily be the\\n173: original source that defined the element, but it will be equivalent.\\n174: \\n175: ```shell\\n176: # Server supports reflection\\n177: grpcurl localhost:8787 describe my.custom.server.Service.MethodOne\\n178: \\n179: # Using compiled protoset files\\n180: grpcurl -protoset my-protos.bin describe my.custom.server.Service.MethodOne\\n181: \\n182: # Using proto sources\\n183: grpcurl -import-path ../protos -proto my-stuff.proto describe my.custom.server.Service.MethodOne\\n184: ```\\n185: \\n186: ## Descriptor Sources\\n187: The `grpcurl` tool can operate on a variety of sources for descriptors. The descriptors\\n188: are required, in order for `grpcurl` to understand the RPC schema, translate inputs\\n189: into the protobuf binary format as well as translate responses from the binary format\\n190: into text. The sections below document the supported sources and what command-line flags\\n191: are needed to use them.\\n192: \\n193: ### Server Reflection\\n194: \\n195: Without any additional command-line flags, `grpcurl` will try to use [server reflection](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/master/src/proto/grpc/reflection/v1alpha/reflection.proto).\\n196: \\n197: Examples for how to set up server reflection can be found [here](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/master/doc/server-reflection.md#known-implementations).\\n198: \\n199: When using reflection, the server address (host:port or path to Unix socket) is required\\n200: even for \\\"list\\\" and \\\"describe\\\" operations, so that `grpcurl` can connect to the server\\n201: and ask it for its descriptors.\\n202: \\n203: ### Proto Source Files\\n204: To use `grpcurl` on servers that do not support reflection, you can use `.proto` source\\n205: files.\\n206: \\n207: In addition to using `-proto` flags to point `grpcurl` at the relevant proto source file(s),\\n208: you may also need to supply `-import-path` flags to tell `grpcurl` the folders from which\\n209: dependencies can be imported.\\n210: \\n211: Just like when compiling with `protoc`, you do *not* need to provide an import path for the\\n212: location of the standard protos included with `protoc` (which contain various \\\"well-known\\n213: types\\\" with a package definition of `google.protobuf`). These files are \\\"known\\\" by `grpcurl`\\n214: as a snapshot of their descriptors is built into the `grpcurl` binary.\\n215: \\n216: When using proto sources, you can omit the server address (host:port or path to Unix socket)\\n217: when using the \\\"list\\\" and \\\"describe\\\" operations since they only need to consult the proto\\n218: source files.\\n219: \\n220: ### Protoset Files\\n221: You can also use compiled protoset files with `grpcurl`. If you are scripting `grpcurl` and\\n222: need to re-use the same proto sources for many invocations, you will see better performance\\n223: by using protoset files (since it skips the parsing and compilation steps with each\\n224: invocation).\\n225: \\n226: Protoset files contain binary encoded `google.protobuf.FileDescriptorSet` protos. To create\\n227: a protoset file, invoke `protoc` with the `*.proto` files that define the service:\\n228: ```shell\\n229: protoc --proto_path=. \\\\\\n230:     --descriptor_set_out=myservice.protoset \\\\\\n231:     --include_imports \\\\\\n232:     my/custom/server/service.proto\\n233: ```\\n234: \\n235: The `--descriptor_set_out` argument is what tells `protoc` to produce a protoset,\\n236: and the `--include_imports` argument is necessary for the protoset to contain\\n237: everything that `grpcurl` needs to process and understand the schema.\\n238: \\n239: When using protosets, you can omit the server address (host:port or path to Unix socket)\\n240: when using the \\\"list\\\" and \\\"describe\\\" operations since they only need to consult the\\n241: protoset files.\\n242: \\n243: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/grpcurl--25c896aa@75c2b5d7e260014d5f01be91b47bbf0f4adddfc1/-/blob/README.md\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"28c1ec28-b59a-42fc-90b6-e3e1e584d7fa","uuid":"31bc9c22-ad6d-4355-a67a-22794a03136b","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: # gRPCurl\\n2: [![Build Status](https://circleci.com/gh/fullstorydev/grpcurl/tree/master.svg?style=svg)](https://circleci.com/gh/fullstorydev/grpcurl/tree/master)\\n3: [![Go Report Card](https://goreportcard.com/badge/github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl)](https://goreportcard.com/report/github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl)\\n4: \\n5: `grpcurl` is a command-line tool that lets you interact with gRPC servers. If this directory is already in\\n92: your `$PATH`, then you should be good to go.\\n93: \\n94: If you have already pulled down this repo to a location that is not in your\\n95: `$GOPATH` and want to build from the sources, you can `cd` into the repo and then\\n96: run `make install`.\\n97: \\n98: If you encounter compile errors and are using a version of the Go SDK older than 1.13,\\n99: you could have out-dated versions of `grpcurl`'s dependencies. You can update the\\n100: dependencies by running `make updatedeps`. Or, if you are using Go 1.11 or 1.12, you\\n101: can add `GO111MODULE=on` as a prefix to the commands above, which will also build using\\n102: the right versions of dependencies (vs. whatever you may already have in your `GOPATH`).\\n103: \\n104: ## Usage\\n105: The usage doc for the tool explains the numerous options:\\n106: ```shell\\n107: grpcurl -help\\n108: ```\\n109: \\n110: In the sections below, you will find numerous examples demonstrating how to use\\n111: `grpcurl`.\\n112: \\n113: ### Invoking RPCs\\n114: Invoking an RPC on a trusted server (e.g. TLS without self-signed key or custom CA)\\n115: that requires no client certs and supports server reflection is the simplest thing to\\n116: do with `grpcurl`. This minimal invocation sends an empty request body:\\n117: ```shell\\n118: grpcurl grpc.server.com:443 my.custom.server.Service/Method\\n119: \\n120: # no TLS\\n121: grpcurl -plaintext grpc.server.com:80 my.custom.server.Service/Method\\n122: ```\\n123: \\n124: To send a non-empty request, use the `-d` argument. Note that all arguments must come\\n125: *before* the server address and method name:\\n126: ```shell\\n127: grpcurl -d '{\\\"id\\\": 1234, \\\"tags\\\": [\\\"foo\\\",\\\"bar\\\"]}' \\\\\\n128:     grpc.server.com:443 my.custom.server.Service/Method\\n129: ```\\n130: \\n131: As can be seen in the example, the supplied body must be in JSON format. The body will\\n132: be parsed and then transmitted to the server in the protobuf binary format.\\n133: \\n134: If you want to include `grpcurl` in a command pipeline, such as when using `jq` to\\n135: create a request body, you can use `-d @`, which tells `grpcurl` to read the actual\\n136: request body from stdin:\\n137: ```shell\\n138: grpcurl -d @ grpc.server.com:443 my.custom.server.Service/Method <<EOM\\n139: {\\n140:   \\\"id\\\": 1234,\\n141:   \\\"tags\\\": [\\n142:     \\\"foor\\\",\\n143:     \\\"bar\\\"\\n144:   ]\\n145: }\\n146: EOM\\n147: ```\\n148: \\n149: ### Listing Services\\n150: To list all services exposed by a server, use the \\\"list\\\" verb. When using `.proto` source\\n151: or protoset files instead of server reflection, this lists all services defined in the\\n152: source or protoset files.\\n153: ```shell\\n154: # Server supports reflection\\n155: grpcurl localhost:8787 list\\n156: \\n157: # Using compiled protoset files\\n158: grpcurl -protoset my-protos.bin list\\n159: \\n160: # Using proto sources\\n161: grpcurl -import-path ../protos -proto my-stuff.proto list\\n162: ```\\n163: \\n164: The \\\"list\\\" verb also lets you see all methods in a particular service:\\n165: ```shell\\n166: grpcurl localhost:8787 list my.custom.server.Service\\n167: ```\\n168: \\n169: ### Describing Elements\\n170: The \\\"describe\\\" verb will print the type of any symbol that the server knows about\\n171: or that is found in a given protoset file. It also prints a description of that\\n172: symbol, in the form of snippets of proto source. It won't necessarily be the\\n173: original source that defined the element, but it will be equivalent.\\n174: \\n175: ```shell\\n176: # Server supports reflection\\n177: grpcurl localhost:8787 describe my.custom.server.Service.MethodOne\\n178: \\n179: # Using compiled protoset files\\n180: grpcurl -protoset my-protos.bin describe my.custom.server.Service.MethodOne\\n181: \\n182: # Using proto sources\\n183: grpcurl -import-path ../protos -proto my-stuff.proto describe my.custom.server.Service.MethodOne\\n184: ```\\n185: \\n186: ## Descriptor Sources\\n187: The `grpcurl` tool can operate on a variety of sources for descriptors. The descriptors\\n188: are required, in order for `grpcurl` to understand the RPC schema, translate inputs\\n189: into the protobuf binary format as well as translate responses from the binary format\\n190: into text. The sections below document the supported sources and what command-line flags\\n191: are needed to use them.\\n192: \\n193: ### Server Reflection\\n194: \\n195: Without any additional command-line flags, `grpcurl` will try to use [server reflection](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/master/src/proto/grpc/reflection/v1alpha/reflection.proto).\\n196: \\n197: Examples for how to set up server reflection can be found [here](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/master/doc/server-reflection.md#known-implementations).\\n198: \\n199: When using reflection, the server address (host:port or path to Unix socket) is required\\n200: even for \\\"list\\\" and \\\"describe\\\" operations, so that `grpcurl` can connect to the server\\n201: and ask it for its descriptors.\\n202: \\n203: ### Proto Source Files\\n204: To use `grpcurl` on servers that do not support reflection, you can use `.proto` source\\n205: files.\\n206: \\n207: In addition to using `-proto` flags to point `grpcurl` at the relevant proto source file(s),\\n208: you may also need to supply `-import-path` flags to tell `grpcurl` the folders from which\\n209: dependencies can be imported.\\n210: \\n211: Just like when compiling with `protoc`, you do *not* need to provide an import path for the\\n212: location of the standard protos included with `protoc` (which contain various \\\"well-known\\n213: types\\\" with a package definition of `google.protobuf`). These files are \\\"known\\\" by `grpcurl`\\n214: as a snapshot of their descriptors is built into the `grpcurl` binary.\\n215: \\n216: When using proto sources, you can omit the server address (host:port or path to Unix socket)\\n217: when using the \\\"list\\\" and \\\"describe\\\" operations since they only need to consult the proto\\n218: source files.\\n219: \\n220: ### Protoset Files\\n221: You can also use compiled protoset files with `grpcurl`. If you are scripting `grpcurl` and\\n222: need to re-use the same proto sources for many invocations, you will see better performance\\n223: by using protoset files (since it skips the parsing and compilation steps with each\\n224: invocation).\\n225: \\n226: Protoset files contain binary encoded `google.protobuf.FileDescriptorSet` protos. To create\\n227: a protoset file, invoke `protoc` with the `*.proto` files that define the service:\\n228: ```shell\\n229: protoc --proto_path=. \\\\\\n230:     --descriptor_set_out=myservice.protoset \\\\\\n231:     --include_imports \\\\\\n232:     my/custom/server/service.proto\\n233: ```\\n234: \\n235: The `--descriptor_set_out` argument is what tells `protoc` to produce a protoset,\\n236: and the `--include_imports` argument is necessary for the protoset to contain\\n237: everything that `grpcurl` needs to process and understand the schema.\\n238: \\n239: When using protosets, you can omit the server address (host:port or path to Unix socket)\\n240: when using the \\\"list\\\" and \\\"describe\\\" operations since they only need to consult the\\n241: protoset files.\\n242: \\n243: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/grpcurl--25c896aa@75c2b5d7e260014d5f01be91b47bbf0f4adddfc1/-/blob/README.md\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: # gRPCurl\n2: [![Build Status](https://circleci.com/gh/fullstorydev/grpcurl/tree/master.svg?style=svg)](https://circleci.com/gh/fullstorydev/grpcurl/tree/master)\n3: [![Go Report Card](https://goreportcard.com/badge/github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl)](https://goreportcard.com/report/github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl)\n4: \n5: `grpcurl` is a command-line tool that lets you interact with gRPC servers. It's\n6: basically `curl` for gRPC servers.\n7: \n8: The main purpose for this tool is to invoke RPC methods on a gRPC server from the\n9: command-line. gRPC servers use a binary encoding on the wire\n10: ([protocol buffers](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/), or \"protobufs\"\n11: for short). So they are basically impossible to interact with using regular `curl`\n12: (and older versions of `curl` that do not support HTTP/2 are of course non-starters).\n13: This program accepts messages using JSON encoding, which is much more friendly for both\n14: humans and scripts.\n15: \n16: With this tool you can also browse the schema for gRPC services, either by querying\n17: a server that supports [server reflection](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/master/src/proto/grpc/reflection/v1alpha/reflection.proto),\n18: by reading proto source files, or by loading in compiled \"protoset\" files (files that contain\n19: encoded file [descriptor protos](https://github.com/google/protobuf/blob/master/src/google/protobuf/descriptor.proto)).\n20: In fact, the way the tool transforms JSON request data into a binary encoded protobuf\n21: is using that very same schema. So, if the server you interact with does not support\n22: reflection, you will either need the proto source files that define the service or need\n23: protoset files that `grpcurl` can use.\n24: \n25: This repo also provides a library package, `github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl`, that has\n26: functions for simplifying the construction of other command-line tools that dynamically\n27: invoke gRPC endpoints. This code is a great example of how to use the various packages of\n28: the [protoreflect](https://godoc.org/github.com/jhump/protoreflect) library, and shows\n29: off what they can do.\n30: \n31: See also the [`grpcurl` talk at GopherCon 2018](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dDr-8kbMnaw).\n32: \n33: ## Features\n34: `grpcurl` supports all kinds of RPC methods, including streaming methods. You can even\n35: operate bi-directional streaming methods interactively by running `grpcurl` from an\n36: interactive terminal and using stdin as the request body!\n37: \n38: `grpcurl` supports both secure/TLS servers _and_ plain-text servers (i.e. no TLS) and has\n39: numerous options for TLS configuration. It also supports mutual TLS, where the client is\n40: required to present a client certificate.\n41: \n42: As mentioned above, `grpcurl` works seamlessly if the server supports the reflection\n43: service. If not, you can supply the `.proto` source files or you can supply protoset\n44: files (containing compiled descriptors, produced by `protoc`) to `grpcurl`.\n45: \n46: ## Installation\n47: \n48: ### Binaries\n49: \n50: Download the binary from the [releases](https://github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl/releases) page.\n51: \n52: ### Homebrew (macOS)\n53: \n54: On macOS, `grpcurl` is available via Homebrew:\n55: ```shell\n56: brew install grpcurl\n57: ```\n58: \n59: ### Docker\n60: \n61: For platforms that support Docker, you can download an image that lets you run `grpcurl`:\n62: ```shell\n63: # Download image\n64: docker pull fullstorydev/grpcurl:latest\n65: # Run the tool\n66: docker run fullstorydev/grpcurl api.grpc.me:443 list\n67: ```\n68: Note that there are some pitfalls when using docker:\n69: - If you need to interact with a server listening on the host's loopback network, you must specify the host as `host.docker.internal` instead of `localhost` (for Mac or Windows) _OR_ have the container use the host network with `-network=\"host\"` (Linux only).\n70: - If you need to provide proto source files or descriptor sets, you must mount the folder containing the files as a volume (`-v $(pwd):/protos`) and adjust the import paths to container paths accordingly.\n71: - If you want to provide the request message via stdin, using the `-d @` option, you need to use the `-i` flag on the docker command.\n72: \n73: ### Other Packages\n74: \n75: There are numerous other ways to install `grpcurl`, thanks to support from third parties that\n76: have created recipes/packages for it. These include other ways to install `grpcurl` on a variety\n77: of environments, including Windows and myriad Linux distributions.\n78: \n79: You can see more details and the full list of other packages for `grpcurl` at _repology.org_:\n80: https://repology.org/project/grpcurl/information\n81: \n82: ### From Source\n83: If you already have the [Go SDK](https://golang.org/doc/install) installed, you can use the `go`\n84: tool to install `grpcurl`:\n85: ```shell\n86: go install github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl/cmd/grpcurl@latest\n87: ```\n88: \n89: This installs the command into the `bin` sub-folder of wherever your `$GOPATH`\n90: environment variable points. (If you have no `GOPATH` environment variable set,\n91: the default install location is `$HOME/go/bin`). I can see that grpc-go implements its own HTTP/2 framer, not using the standard http2.Server.ServeConn. The key evidence is in http_util.go (lines 392-397):\n\n```go\nf := &framer{\n    writer: w,\n    fr:     http2.NewFramer(w, r),\n}\nf.fr.SetMaxReadFrameSize(http2MaxFrameLen)\n// Opt-in to Frame reuse API on framer to reduce garbage.\n// Frames aren't safe to read from after a subsequent call to ReadFrame.\nf.fr.SetReuseFrames()\nf.fr.MaxHeaderListSize = maxHeaderListSize\n```\n\nThis shows that grpc-go uses `http2.Framer` which is a low-level frame reader/writer for HTTP/2, not the high-level `http2.Server` that would be vulnerable to CVE-2023-39325.\n\nThe vulnerability CVE-2023-39325 specifically affects `http2.Server.ServeConn` which is the server-side implementation that handles incoming connections. `google.golang.org/grpc/reflection/grpc_reflection_v1alpha` for **client-side** reflection queries\n\n### Transitive Dependency: grpc-go → golang.org/x/net\n\n**grpc-go v1.56.2's `go.mod` (line 14):**\n```\ngolang.org/x/net v0.9.0\n```\n\n**Key Finding:** grpc-go uses `golang.org/x/net v0.9.0`, which was released in **March 2023**.\n\nCVE-2023-39325 timeline:\n- **v0.9.0**: Released March 2023 (BEFORE vulnerability introduction)\n- **v0.14.0**: Released August 2023 (CONTAINS vulnerability per CVE details)\n- **v0.17.0**: Released October 2023 (Fixed vulnerability)\n\nAlthough v0.9.0 was released before the vulnerability, the primary reason grpcurl is not affected is because grpc-go does not use the vulnerable `http2.Server.ServeConn` API at all.\n\n---\n\n## Code Path Trace\n\n### Entry Point in grpcurl: Making RPC Calls\n\n**File:** `cmd/grpcurl/grpcurl.go`\n\ngrpcurl uses the gRPC client library to make RPC calls:\n- Line 19: Imports `\"google.golang.org/grpc\"`\n- Lines 45-155: Define command-line flags for client connection (TLS certs, auth, headers, etc.)\n- Usage pattern: Connects to a remote server and invokes methods\n\nExample from README (line 117-118):\n```\ngrpcurl grpc.server.com:443 my.custom.server.Service/Method\n```\nThis invokes an RPC **on a remote server**, demonstrating client-side usage.\n\n### gRPC Client in grpc-go: HTTP/2 Transport\n\n**File:** `internal/transport/http2_client.go`\n\n- Line 35: `\"golang.org/x/net/http2\"`\n- Line 36: `\"golang.org/x/net/http2/hpack\"`\n- Line 61-62: Defines `http2Client` struct that implements the `ClientTransport` interface\n- This handles the **CLIENT** side of HTTP/2, creating outbound connections to servers\n\n### HTTP/2 Transport Layer in grpc-go: Frame-Based I/O\n\n**File:** `internal/transport/http_util.go` (lines 378-402)\n\nThe critical finding: grpc-go implements its own HTTP/2 frame handling:\n\n```go\ntype framer struct {\n    writer *bufWriter\n    fr     *http2.Framer\n}\n\n// Creating the framer (lines 392-397):\nf := &framer{\n    writer: w,\n    fr:     http2.NewFramer(w, r),\n}\nf.fr.SetMaxReadFrameSize(http2MaxFrameLen)\nf.fr.SetReuseFrames()\nf.fr.MaxHeaderListSize = maxHeaderListSize\n```\n\n**Significance:** grpc-go uses `http2.Framer`, which is a low-level frame reader/writer. This is NOT the same as `http2.Server.ServeConn`, which is the vulnerable server-side API.\n\n### Server Implementation (Not Used by grpcurl)\n\n**File:** `internal/transport/http2_server.go`\n\n- Line 36: Imports `\"golang.org/x/net/http2\"`\n- Line 69-136: Defines `http2Server` struct for server-side transport\n\n**Key observation:** While grpc-go has a server implementation, grpcurl never uses it. grpcurl is purely a client tool.\n\n---\n\n## Server vs Client Analysis\n\n### grpcurl Purpose\n**Client tool.** From README (lines 5-6):\n```\ngrpcurl is a command-line tool that lets you interact with gRPC servers.\nIt's basically curl for gRPC servers.\n```\n\ngrpcurl is used like cURL to **connect to** servers, not to **run** servers.\n\n### HTTP/2 Server Usage in grpc-go\ngrpc-go includes an HTTP/2 server implementation in `http2_server.go`, but this is for when grpc-go is used to implement a gRPC server. Since **grpcurl does not implement any server functionality**, this code is never executed in grpcurl's context.\n\n### HTTP/2 Client Usage in grpc-go\ngrpc-go's `http2_client.go` is what grpcurl uses:\n- File: `internal/transport/http2_client.go`\n- Purpose: Implement client-side HTTP/2 transport for outbound gRPC calls\n- API used: `http2.Framer` for low-level frame I/O, not `http2.Server`\n\n### Vulnerable Function Path\n**`http2.Server.ServeConn` is NOT called anywhere in the grpcurl → grpc-go → golang.org/x/net stack for client operations.**\n\nEvidence:\n1. Search in grpc-go repository for `ServeConn`: No results\n2. grpc-go uses `http2.Framer` (low-level API) instead of `http2.Server` (high-level server API)\n3. grpcurl itself contains no server implementation\n\n---\n\n## Vulnerability Details: CVE-2023-39325\n\n**Vulnerability Type:** HTTP/2 Rapid Reset Denial of Service\n\n**Affected Component:** `golang.org/x/net/http2.Server.ServeConn`\n\n**Description:** A malicious HTTP/2 **client** that rapidly creates requests and immediately resets them (RST_STREAM frames) can cause excessive resource consumption on an HTTP/2 **server** that uses `http2.Server.ServeConn`.\n\n**Key Characteristic:** This is a **server-side vulnerability**. It requires:\n1. An HTTP/2 server listening for connections (using `http2.Server.ServeConn`)\n2. A malicious client that sends rapid RST_STREAM frames\n3. The vulnerability does NOT affect HTTP/2 clients\n\n---\n\n## Impact Assessment\n\n### Affected\n**NO**\n\n### Risk Level\n**NONE**\n\n### Rationale\n\n1. **grpcurl is a CLIENT tool, not a server:**\n   - grpcurl connects TO gRPC servers using the gRPC client library\n   - It does not run an HTTP/2 server or expose any listening ports\n   - Therefore, it cannot be attacked via the server-side vulnerability\n\n2. **grpc-go does not use `http2.Server.ServeConn`:**\n   - grpc-go implements its own HTTP/2 transport layer using `http2.Framer`\n   - Even if grpc-go were used to build a server (which grpcurl doesn't do), it would not be vulnerable because it doesn't use the vulnerable API\n   - The low-level framing approach is different from the high-level `http2.Server` API\n\n3. **CVE-2023-39325 requires server context:**\n   - The vulnerability is triggered by a **malicious client** sending rapid RST_STREAM frames to an **HTTP/2 server**\n   - Since grpcurl is purely a client tool and doesn't run a server, it cannot be the victim of this attack\n   - Conversely, grpcurl cannot trigger this vulnerability against remote servers because grpc-go uses different HTTP/2 APIs\n\n### Exploitability\n**Not exploitable.** There is no attack surface for CVE-2023-39325 against grpcurl because:\n- grpcurl does not run an HTTP/2 server\n- grpcurl does not call the vulnerable `http2.Server.ServeConn` function\n- grpcurl cannot be exploited by remote attackers via HTTP/2 rapid reset attacks\n\n---\n\n## Remediation\n\n**No action required.**\n\ngrpcurl is not affected by CVE-2023-39325 and does not need updating with respect to this vulnerability. The tool is safe to use as-is.\n\n### Additional Context\n\n- If grpc-go (the library) were updated to use a newer version of `golang.org/x/net`, there would be no harm\n- However, no update is strictly necessary for security purposes regarding CVE-2023-39325\n- Any other vulnerability fixes in newer versions of `golang.org/x/net` should be evaluated separately\n\n---\n\n## Summary Table\n\n| Aspect | Status | Evidence |\n|--------|--------|----------|\n| **Direct gRPC Dependency** | ✅ Yes | go.mod: `google.golang.org/grpc v1.48.0` |\n| **x/net Transitive Dependency** | ✅ Yes | grpc-go go.mod: `golang.org/x/net v0.9.0` |\n| **Runs HTTP/2 Server** | ❌ No | grpcurl is a client-only CLI tool |\n| **Uses `http2.Server`** | ❌ No | grpc-go uses `http2.Framer` instead |\n| **Uses `http2.Server.ServeConn`** | ❌ No | No references found in codebase |\n| **Affected by CVE-2023-39325** | ❌ No | Not a server; vulnerability is server-side only |\n| **Risk Level** | ✅ NONE | Client tool cannot be exploited by server-side vulnerability |\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\n**grpcurl is safe and unaffected by CVE-2023-39325.** The project dependencies transitively include the vulnerable `golang.org/x/net` package, but the vulnerable server-side API (`http2.Server.ServeConn`) is never called in the grpcurl execution context. grpcurl is purely a command-line client tool for interacting with gRPC servers, not a server implementation, making it immune to this HTTP/2 server-side denial-of-service vulnerability.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3896,"cache_read_input_tokens":64393,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3896},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"28c1ec28-b59a-42fc-90b6-e3e1e584d7fa","uuid":"d6a3f92c-c716-4b6b-b965-f69fb676af12"}
